Spring and Autumn

Saying "Five" 245

— Qi Ling

Reading Mr. Xing Zhi's discussion of "Three" in this publication, I can't help but feel that there is also a need to discuss "Five." "Three" and "Five" are both nouns for numbers, and the construction of their characters is very similar. The number "Five" is larger than "Three," but in China, I feel that "Five" is even more worthy of remembrance.

Sun Yat-sen originally created the Five-Power Constitution, using the character "Five." It is said that with the Five-Power Constitution, the country can be revitalized and governed, and this "Five" character becomes extraordinary. Foreigners mock our compatriots for lacking perseverance, calling it "five-minute enthusiasm." Here, we feel that this "Five" character is not good and contains insults.

Due to the continuous oppression of foreign aggression, many anniversaries related to "Five" have been added. After "May Seventh," "May Ninth," and "May Thirtieth," the anniversaries with "Five" are all considered inauspicious terms. There are many other anniversaries related to "Five," such as "May First" Labor Day and "May Fourth" Student Movement.

Asia, Europe, America, Australia, and Africa are called the Five Continents; the Pacific, Indian, Atlantic, Southern, and Arctic Oceans are called the Five Oceans; Yellow, White, Black, Red, and Brown are called the Five Races; Han, Manchu, Mongol, Hui, and Tibetan are called the Five Ethnic Groups; Mount Tai, Mount Hua, Mount Heng, Mount Heng, and Mount Song are called the Five Sacred Mountains; the Book of Poetry, the Book of Documents, the Book of Changes, the Book of Rites, and the Spring and Autumn Annals are called the Five Classics; Benevolence, Righteousness, Propriety, Wisdom, and Trustworthiness are called the Five Constant Virtues; Gong, Shang, Jiao, Zhi, and Yu are called the Five Tones; East, West, North, South, and Center are called the Five Directions; Branding, Nose Cutting, Foot Cutting, Castration, and Death Penalty are called the Five Punishments; Metal, Wood, Water, Fire, and Earth are called the Five Elements; Liver, Heart, Spleen, Lungs, and Kidneys are called the Five Viscera; Ears, Eyes, Mouth, Nose, and Tongue are called the Five Senses. There are too many applications of the word "Five" to describe them all at once. In modern times, Britain, the United States, Japan, France, and Italy are called the Five Powers. Soviet Russia has a Five-Year Plan, and the prize money for aviation lotteries must be 500,000. The Fifth Plenary Session is about to open. I hope that the ruling gentlemen will set a grand plan as soon as possible, so that there will be no more disunity. Let everyone devote their five points of strength, become proficient in the five kinds of weapons, organize their five armies, respectfully spread the five teachings, respectfully use the five powers, sacrifice five feet, shed blood five steps, and engage in a final five-minute duel with the enemy. Only then can we protect our five ethnic groups, defend our five lands, and make our five-thousand-year-old Chinese ancient country stand out among the five continents and be listed among the five powers. Then, there will be no more humiliating and power-losing events such as the five treaty ports.

Rambling Talk on Cartoons 246

— Qian Yun writes, Lian Liang draws

丨They in the Summer Heat丨

In this summer of 1933, if you don't do something utterly fashionable, you risk being considered wronged, affected, or foolish. Chewing ice and taking a drive are nothing. Going to an air-conditioned room, a swimming pool, or Qingdao is what shows you're modernized. The air conditioning freezes Mr. Wang's teeth until they chatter against each other. He takes a packet of herbal tea that night, saying it's "xieyi" (carefree). Swimming pools in Gaoqiao and Hongkou are even more crowded. Anyway, even if you don't know how to swim, it's good to soak your skin. Then take a few photos in your swimming suit. Some people are so obsessed that they even swim in the bathtub, not caring about the water splashing everywhere, but saying that the water here has absolutely no salty taste. Speaking of Qingdao, Mogan Mountain, and Putuo for summering, of course, these are fashionable, luxurious, and comfortable things. A tanned man's face is healthy, a tanned woman's... is beautiful. But these places seem to be specially prepared for the rich in Shanghai to enjoy themselves, regardless of whether these places are truly enjoyable. Only one day, I happened to stand in front of a blacksmith shop in Nanshi for a long time, watching two workers blacksmithing. The red-hot iron block was taken out of the fire hole with tongs and beaten alternately, up and down, from a thick block to a thin sheet. The transformation from red-hot to gray in that instant was quite interesting. But needless to say, the two men were covered in sweat, and the drops covered their eyes. They couldn't extend a third hand to wipe them away, letting them drip down. The child carrying the furnace next to them had a face that was especially red and black, illuminated by the firelight. They themselves wouldn't, but I imagined for them that if they were to go to an air-conditioned room, a swimming pool, or Qingdao at this time, wouldn't they... Oh! Don't say it, saying it would make most people laugh their heads off.

There were no other thoughts on this day, and thinking about it would never end. I only felt that the weather had become particularly cool because of it!

Madam Wang, the Teacher 247

— Zhao Ziming

Last time, I introduced Teacher Wang. Now, let me introduce his wife.

She came from a magistrate's family. When Teacher Wang was serving as a secretary, the magistrate loved him for his youth and handsomeness, so he made him his son-in-law. She is very obese, but she accompanies the medicine pot every other day, much like the sickly "Lin Daiyu." Now, her temples are as white as frost, and she still rubs on shimmering hair growth oil. Her three-inch golden lilies are shod in blood-red embroidered shoes. She is truly "old in years, but not in heart"!

She knows "Kong Yiji" and "Hua Sanqian," but she only knows about twenty characters in total.

One day, she had a get-rich dream and bought a lottery ticket. She treasured it very much. When the draw came, she realized that she had bought an old ticket from last year's draw. Teacher Wang loves money as his life, so she didn't dare to tell him. This is also the benefit of "a woman's lack of talent is a virtue"!

In the winter, when it snowed heavily and the road was muddy, she went out to buy soy sauce and slipped on the snow. She didn't want passersby to help her and slowly got up on her own because "men and women should not touch hands."

Sometimes, she would cry with her head in her hands, pointing at Teacher Wang and complaining: "I married you for a lifetime and haven't had a happy day, haven't worn a new dress, and haven't eaten a peaceful meal. My life is so thin!" In fact, Teacher Wang used to be popular too. How could she not have enjoyed happiness? I can't help but call out injustice for Teacher Wang! But her purpose in marrying Teacher Wang was only for good clothes and good food!

When she saw women cutting their hair, she strongly disapproved, scolding them as demons, neither like nuns nor like monks!

Later, after Teacher Wang died of cholera, she lay on his corpse and cried all day long. Soon, she also contracted cholera and followed Teacher Wang to the underworld. It can be considered that "they were shoulder to shoulder in life and became flounders in death."

Leg Talk 248

— Zhang Xianling

The even number of legs is simply always a double number. The Shang Yang in the primer has three legs, the Long Xuhu in the Investiture of the Gods has one leg, and Liu Hai's mount is a three-legged toad. However, these strange legs with different numbers have no confirmed textual research and are mostly regarded as folktales, so they cannot be considered as odd legs.

Human beings are divided into three types: male, female, and neither male nor female. Usually, there are two types: male and female. All three types of people have two legs. Since the beginning of history, there has never been anyone seen with one or three legs, unless they were injured and had one leg amputated or completely amputated. However, people's legs have clever names: iron legs, big legs, long legs, beautiful legs, fast legs, etc. Things in the world are often unexpected. In the current society where capitalism is rampant, people's legs have actually become commercial advertising competitions. Like the movie advertisements in various newspapers, women's bare legs occupy the eyes of movie fans one by one. Not only is this the case in commerce, but it is also the case in gender issues. The women seen on the street, when you don't pay attention to their faces, those two legs have already invaded your eyes. In the summer, women even bare their legs and wear shorts. This kind of policy often makes Liu Xiahui's heart flutter, and he no longer dares to say that form is emptiness.

I heard that American movie stars draw many human heads and other flowers and plants on their legs as decoration. Our Chinese women only have the trend of bare legs. Perhaps they will follow in the footsteps of American movie stars in the future. If the use of legs can be developed to the highest peak, then the exchange value can also flourish arbitrarily. We will always see the mystery of legs in the future.

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 249

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Fifteen: The guest leaves with shyness, and tender feelings stir. The smiling person comes to visit, and old grievances and bad news cause sorrow.

A joyful atmosphere filled the room. Zhao Ziqiang and Yang Guizhi's shy expressions also dissolved in the joy. Huang Manying looked at this scene and smiled at Guizhi. "Today, our efforts were not in vain. I hope that from now on, you will make appointments to come here yourselves. Don't travel dozens of miles to find me, just to eat a bowl of tangyuan." Guizhi lowered her head, only smiling as she ate, without saying anything. Huang Manying said sternly, "Yang, don't be shy. I'm talking to you seriously." Guizhi smiled, "Why should I be shy? If I were shy, I wouldn't come." Tian Qing reached out and gently patted Zhao Ziqiang's arm twice, laughing. "Did you hear that? People aren't shy, are you still shy?" Zhao Ziqiang smiled, "Who can be like you guys?" Tian Qing said to Huang Manying, "Did you hear that? He said he can't be like you guys. Your opposite is us. He also knows to say 'us'." Zhao Ziqiang said, "Xiao Tian, ​​you're getting better and better at talking. I can say you're not weak." Just as they were saying this, Huang Manying suddenly frowned, repeatedly calling out, "What to do? What to do?" Tian Qing was startled and stood up. He asked him, "What's wrong with you?" Manying walked towards the outside of the private room, beckoning to him. Tian Qing had no choice but to follow him out. After a while, he stumbled back in three steps and two steps, grabbed the military cap on the table, and stumbled out again. Zhao Ziqiang thought that Huang Manying had something inconvenient, so he left. Tian Qing, of course, followed to serve him. Guizhi sat on the side, thinking the same thing in her heart. Although the two of them had left, she sitting here alone was a bit awkward, but looking at Huang...

Manying's appearance, she couldn't stop them. So, she watched them leave, and she just held the tangyuan bowl, only lowering her head to drink the broth. (182)

Short Story

The First Autumn Rain (Part 2) 250

— Hu Liwen

"Xiuer! 丨丨" My mother's voice was a little trembling, "Don't go there anymore! Just stay at home, we can make a living by farming, why do you have to suffer from other people's temper!"

"Really! Little brother, it's better not to go there!"

My sister echoed with this sentence. I looked at her smiling face, wanting to argue, but sorrow filled my throat, and I could no longer speak.

My sister and I went to the living room to eat. There were only the two of us at the table. My sister told me: My mother hasn't eaten for half a month, drinking only thin rice porridge every day. Today, because I came back, my sister specially bought a pot of wine to welcome me. She never liked drinking, but today, to accompany me, she drank several cups in a row. The corners of her eyebrows turned a faint red. She smiled and talked to me about the situation after we parted. I listened, I drank wine, but I didn't say a word.

Ah Hua ran in panting. In the past, I liked it very much. I often took it to play in the wild, to bathe in the stream. Now, it seems to be estranged from me. It glared at me and turned to my sister, first sniffing her feet, then sniffing her calves, then raising its two front paws and placing them on her knees, looking up at her, its tail wagging non-stop. My sister reached out and stroked its head, smiling and pointing at me, asking it:

"Hua! Do you still recognize your little master?"

As if understanding my sister's words, Ah Hua glanced at me and ran over to me, wagging its tail and rubbing against my legs, showing affection. I picked up a piece of tofu for it. It stood up like a child, its front paws hanging down, its head raised, and from between my chopsticks, it swallowed the piece of tofu into its stomach.

Suddenly, my mother called me urgently in the room, her voice obviously different. I hurried in. My mother was already sitting up, and a person was standing in front of her. I recognized him as the accountant from our factory. I didn't know what was going on and was about to go forward and ask him. Suddenly, he turned around, grabbed my arm like a fierce god, and dragged me out, shouting:

"Hurry! Come back with me! The boss is throwing a temper there. He doesn't allow you to take leave, how dare you be so bold and run back on your own?"

My mother shouted loudly, "Xiuer! My child! Don't go! Don't go! Is he here to catch you? Beat him to death!" She jumped off the bed and grabbed my clothes. My sister also hugged my waist. Even Ah Hua bit my trouser leg. They cried, shouted, and yelled, pulling me inward together. I was pulled down by them.

Opening my eyes, I was still lying in bed. The electric light in the room laughed coldly at me. The sound of the first autumn rain burst outside the window. Cold sweat soaked my short shirt. I recalled the dream I just had. I was both happy and sorrowful and angry. I really wanted to immediately

丨At least tomorrow morning丨丨 set off to go home, but is it possible? The first time I asked for leave, it was not approved. The second time I asked for leave, I was scolded. Who would dare to try again? And tomorrow I have to continue my struggle.

"The flames of the electric light scorch my body; the sound of rain outside the window shatters the strings of my heart.

I wish to turn into the storm of autumn,

Sprinkling on the door of my hometown!"

I murmured. My tears fell again.

Commercial News

Gold, Commodity Prices, and Stocks Fall; Premium Recovers to Four Dollars and Six Cents 251

丨Situation Lingers, Many Consolidation Patterns丨

Yesterday, the gold market saw mixed signals. Although overseas reports indicated a slight rise in silver prices in England and the United States, exchange rates turned downward. The forward silver price at the Metal Exchange rose by nine haos to one li and nine fen, but there was little demand. In addition, American cotton fell by fourteen pounds, American wheat shrank by one and three-quarters, and stocks fell by more than one dollar. This improved sentiment. The opening price for raw gold was 827 yuan, a slight dip due to selling by Daxing, Yongheng, and Xing. After the opening, banks dumped, and the exchange market hardened and turned downward. HSBC's listed prices were announced, with no changes in shillings or US dollars. At this time, the market turned flat. Bank dumping briefly caused a slight delay in the rise, but ultimately fell back as banks were still willing to supply at high prices. The situation lingered, with many consolidation patterns. The opening price in the afternoon fell, due to a Reuters report that the American Bankers Association convention had agreed to extend loans to industry and commerce and cooperate with the National Recovery Administration within a sound business scope. Although this did not have a major impact, it turned sentiment weary. Afterwards, the market gradually became peaceful, with little trading. The situation lingered, and rose again near closing. The long-strained bond market shows a slight recovery

The process is one of gradual increase from a low point.

Trading is relatively lively.

There are whispers of a comprehensive plan requiring significant funds, which will inevitably lead to the issuance of new public bonds to inject capital and address cotton and wheat problems. The market, encouraged by the conference's progress, saw a shift in sentiment, with prices initially falling before rising. Wind Disaster's Impact on Nantong Cotton Not Significant 264

Regarding the recent wind disaster's impact on Nantong cotton production, we received news from a friend in Nantong today. The strong winds in Nantong, after observation, caused only minor damage, such as some shedding of already-opened cotton fibers and new bolls, and some flooding of cotton fields along the river. The estimated maximum loss is only about 4-5%. However, the two counties of Qidong and Hai站门 have seen reduced cotton yields due to the dry summer, which hindered cotton seedling development. People from Baoshan say that the wind disaster's impact was not significant because about one-third of the bolls have already opened, and even unopened bolls are already quite large, making them less likely to be blown off. However, the current tender bolls may be somewhat diminished.

Foreign Rice Trading Stalled 270

| Inventory: 267,837 Sacks |

Future arrivals will be abundant, and the market will be oversupplied. Currently, new Ke Xian rice is arriving, so there is no need to focus on foreign rice, and they are determined not to buy unless prices fall. Therefore, both sides are waiting and watching.

Autumn is approaching, but there is still no news or demand in the black sheet iron market. Overall, the market situation is stagnant and unlikely to improve in the short term. Northern ports, such as Tianjin, Qingdao, Yantai, Beiping, and Zhangjiakou, lack demand due to tight credit or unstable conditions. Local enamel factories are saturated, so they are also buying less. The overall trend is not optimistic.

Over Two Thousand Boxes of US Tinplate Offered 278

Recently, with the price of US tinplate relatively cheap, trading houses and factories find it cost-effective. Therefore, over the past few days, more than 2,300 boxes have been offered. 90-pound tinplate without iron casing is offered at prices ranging from 16.35 yuan to 16.5 yuan. 90-pound tinplate with iron casing is offered at prices ranging from 16.85 yuan to 17.1 yuan. However, only over 380 boxes were traded. The prices of 180-pound and 200-pound tinplate have seen slight fluctuations, with limited transactions. 180-pound tinplate is offered at 34 yuan, and 200-pound tinplate is offered at 39 yuan. Local traders are also buying some 200-pound small and large quantities of Huisi iron at prices ranging from 31.5 yuan to 32 yuan. It is reported that the Ningbo bamboo shoot factories are asking for more information, making trading quite considerable.

Free Talk

About Occupation 279

— Du Heng

Because I have no occupation, as usual, having one would be a huge exception. That is to say, because there is no job to lose, I have never personally experienced the suffering of unemployment among the various pains of life. It is invisibly dispersed in the continuous struggle with poverty; when integrated into zero, one gradually gets used to it, as if this is one's duty in life. However, I do not therefore fail to express a kind of envy, or even jealousy, towards people with fixed occupations, and from this arises a kind of aversion. This is indeed a strange psychology.

In China today, the most stable and secure occupations are probably those eating foreign food, that is, the so-called comprador class and its subordinates. The aversion to these people stems precisely from the fact that their occupations are too stable and too secure, which is even greater than that towards other people.

Often, during the free time from office work, in places like the Bund, there are many well-dressed young gentlemen with newspapers, jumping on trams, not buying tickets, but indifferently saying "Season" or just gently shaking their heads to indicate an exception, and then opening small newspapers to find stimulating headlines. Whenever I see this kind of scene, I don't know why, but I say in my heart: "I hope everyone in the world has no occupation."

Of course, I also know that widespread unemployment is hitting our intellectual or semi-intellectual classes. Some people who want stability and security but cannot obtain them are suffering even more than long-term unemployed vagrants. They are anxious, they are scheming, they pay more attention to classified ads in newspapers than to racy social news, they beautifully say "There is no way out" everywhere, they even ask newspaper editors for "elixirs" to cure poverty. Previously, smart editors were accustomed to using knowledge, ability, and experience to perfunctorily tell you to be patient, to endure hardship, and to not hesitate to invest more capital. Whether this "elixir" is effective or not, those who have tried it naturally know, and there is no need for me to say more. Recently, the situation is different. Editors have already discovered the truth that solving the entire society is a prerequisite. But their words are too beautiful: Do not seek a way out for yourself, seek a way out for the masses. A young person who is eager to obtain immediate stability and security often only has the feeling of swallowing an empty dumpling when receiving this truth.

A truly promising young person, whipped by such serious life, will understand this truth sooner than a smart editor. And those friends who ask for "elixirs," once their luck shines, earning thirty or fifty taels of silver, getting a raise every year and a promotion every two years, and after thirty years, they can go home to retire and still receive silver, at that time, they will surely put on a new-fashioned gentleman's tone to demonstrate to us long-term unemployed vagrants, buy Season tickets as usual, and buy small newspapers as usual.

They will never think of the four words "There is no way out" again, because in their view, society is entirely stable because they have an occupation.

From "In Defense of Translation" to Lou's Translation of "European Literature in the Twentieth Century" 280

— Mu Mutian

Mr. Luo Wen, in "In Defense of Translation," said the following:

"If a translation is bad, most of the responsibility certainly lies with the translator, but the reading public and the publishing industry, especially critics, should also bear some of the responsibility. To remedy this decline, we must have correct criticism, pointing out the bad and rewarding the good."

Due to editorial work, I happened to compare Mr. Lou Jiannan's translation of "European Literature in the Twentieth Century" (New Life Publishing) with a Japanese translation. Naturally, there are many mistranslations. Because I only glanced through it, I immediately discovered the following strange phenomena.

On page 14, under "Maxime Du Camp" is a note: "(Maxim du Kahn)". I was very strange, because I searched everywhere, but I couldn't find this person. There is a Frenchman, Maxime du Camp, who was a friend of Flaubert. There is also a poet named Gustave Kahn, who is Jewish. "Maxim du Kahn" I don't know who this person is. I'm afraid the original name attached by Mr. Lou is fabricated.

On page 199, there is a statement "Among such novels, the most outstanding are the immortal works of Louis Bertrand, recently selected by the Academy (Translator: presumably referring to the Russian Communist Academy to which the author belongs)." I think the "Academie" here should refer to the French Academy. Although the Soviet Union is called a land of developed arts and culture, it would not compile a collection of imperialist writers, would it? I don't know why Mr. Lou made such indiscriminate annotations?

On page 223, there is "In the early twentieth century, France stepped into a new era of its history, large-scale (metallurgical) industry grew: the power of financial capital was strengthened; the ideology of imperialism was strong." At first glance. I felt quite puzzled. "France stepped into a new era of its history," what is going on? I couldn't help but look at the Japanese translation. It was not France, but France. I really don't know how Mr. Lou was so negligent, and translated it without even looking clearly at the context of the original text. This is too irresponsible.

On page 240, there is a book title "The Non-Burning Forest." At first glance, I also felt strange. Because I don't know, I have never heard that Romain Rolland has written that book. On closer inspection, it was originally Volume 9 of "Jean-Christophe". Its original French name is Le Buisson Ardent. "Ardent" means "burning" or "like burning". Where could I find the word "non-burning"? I thought the Japanese translation was wrong, so I checked the Japanese translation, and it turned out to be "burning again cluster". "Again" is an auxiliary verb indicating "past". It is not an auxiliary verb indicating negation and cancellation. I don't know why Mr. Lou doesn't understand this point of grammar?

On page 288, there is a sentence "Finally, the people delegated the words of decision." This sentence made me confused again. Looking at the original Japanese translation, it turned out to mean "Finally, entrust the words of decision to the people."

On page 241, there is a sentence "A seemingly new but not new intellectual class." What is the so-called "seemingly new but not new"? I doubted it. Looking at the Japanese translation, it means "a new and completely different intellectual class."

On page 284, there is: "I also want to speed it up," but the original meaning is: "I add a sentence." The Japanese translation of this sentence is very superficial. I don't know why Mr. Lou made such a big mistake?

On page 284, there is: "Our victory is the same as Caesar's destruction, vainly dreaming of enslaving one country and enslaving another country's crown prince's stove." How to explain this? I checked the Japanese translation. Then I checked Barbusse's original French text again. The French and Japanese are not very similar. According to the Japanese translation, it can be said that "Our victory is the same as destroying Caesar's | | vainly dreaming of making this nation a slave and making that nation a slave's crown prince's | | lair." I don't know why Mr. Lou translated it so strangely? This is not only not "faithful" but also not "smooth" and not "understandable" | | What is the reason?

The above are a few strange mistakes encountered during a casual browsing, missing some. Except for the error on page 284 at the end, which may be excusable (because the Japanese may be a bit difficult), the others should not be wrong. As long as you have studied Japanese for one or two years, you will definitely not be wrong. But Mr. Lou actually made a mistake!

After reading Mr. Luo Wen's article, I felt a slight sense of responsibility, | although I am not a critic | so I reported the strange phenomena I obtained from a casual browsing. I think this is beneficial for both translators and readers.

For the sake of a good future for the Chinese translation community, I think everyone should do this kind of inspection and criticism work. But it should be done with a calm, sincere, and friendly attitude, and should not be an attack, ridicule, or scolding.

Ma Zhiyuan's Zaju Plays 281

— Zheng Zhenduo

A few days ago, Mr. Zhao Jingshen discussed Ma Zhiyuan's zaju plays in "Free Talk"; there are two errors in the article that are worth mentioning. First, Mr. Zhao cited four short poems by Ma, thinking that they were the embryos of Ma's four plays such as "Meng Haoran Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow". This is a hardly believable judgment. Who knows whether Ma's short poems were written before or after the zaju plays? The expression of broad-minded world-weariness in the short poems is a common idea of ​​general Yuan qu artists; how can it be strongly pointed out that Ma first had the embryo possessed by these short poems, and then developed it into a zaju play? If this is the case, there are also quite a few poems in Yuan people's short poems that praise Chen Tuan, Meng Haoran, etc. Could they also be the embryos of Ma's zaju plays? There are the most short poems by Yuan and Ming people, singing about the stories of Cui and Zhang (Yongxi Yuefu has a hundred "Little Peach Red", singing about the affairs of the West Chamber; the "Sai Zhaoyunfei Little Songs" published during the Chenghua period also has many articles singing about the affairs of the West Chamber.) Could they also be the embryos of Wang Shifu's "Romance of the West Chamber"? I think that in studying a writer's works, except for clearly knowing the exact year in which his works were produced, it is very difficult to determine whether a certain article is the embryo of a certain work, or whether a certain work is developed from a certain article or poem; and it is even more impossible to insist that they must be the embryo of a zaju play because the short poems are short. We can only say that Ma's short poems are the same in thought as his zaju plays | | of course, they are from the same writer, and the thoughts will naturally not be very different.

Second, Mr. Zhao unconditionally believed in Wang Guowei's "Catalogue of Music," thinking that the play "Meng Haoran Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow" was written by Ma Zhiyuan. In fact, Ma had never written this play at all. We cannot find a play called "Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow" in Ma's repertoire in the oldest records of "Record of Ghosts" and "Taihe Zheng Yin Pu". Forcing this play to be the author of Ma's work began with Xijizi's "Selected Ancient and Modern Zaju Plays" in the Ming Dynasty. Wang Guowei added this play to Ma's works based on Xijizi's saying. It is ridiculous to say that the "Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow" play recorded by Xijizi was originally written by Prince Zhou Xian (Zhu You). Prince Xian's play was written in the seventh year of Xuande, with a preface explaining the purpose of writing this play in great detail, and of course it would not be a copy or adaptation of Ma's play. (Xijizi's "Selected Zaju Plays" is in the collection of the Peking Library; Zhou Xianwang's "Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow" can be seen in the Commercial Press edition of "Shemotuo Studio Qu Cong") We cannot know why Xijizi insisted on putting this hat on that head; could it be that he also read Ma's short poems and felt that some of the short poems were the embryos of this play? In the Ming Dynasty, such forgery of author names was commonplace, especially in sanqu and drama songs. (Fangben such as "Wu Yu Cui Ya" are the most absurd, with many errors in the author's name.) We must carefully analyze them, and we will be greatly deceived if we are not careful. Many of the errors in Wang Guowei's "Catalogue of Music" are often obtained in this way. It should not be a boring job to correct the errors of Wang and other Ming people with today's correct knowledge and compile another "General Catalogue of Chinese Opera" (there are even more errors in the "General Catalogue of Quhai" by Datong).

Woman (16) 282

— Shen Congwen

"I'm very happy. I thank you."

On those two sentences, I savored them for a long time, and it was precisely to put myself into all the past days.

After a while, the woman said:

"I'm also very happy."

"I think you are much younger, even younger than when I saw you by the sea in Shandong." "Really?"

"Look into my eyes, look, and you will understand how your beauty is reflected in a man's surprise!" "But you didn't in the past | never surprised by any beauty, nor surrendered by any gentleness."

"Did I say that?"

"Although I didn't say it, there are such facts."

He leaned closer to her, gently put his other hand on her shoulder, and brought his head close to her temple.

"I am very ashamed when I think of my own confusion."

She turned her face away, covering up her sadness, but gently said:

"Look, how beautiful the village below is!"

The man, like a child, walked in front of her, searching her face, and she lowered her head, no longer speaking. He wanted to hug her, but she ran forward. In front was the short wall of the cemetery whose surname was unknown. She stood there motionless. He rushed forward and squeezed both of her hands tightly. Face to face, neither of them had anything to say. They both seemed to be touching something, and they were speechless, unable to say anything more.

The woman rubbed a white hand against the man's cheek and arm, "Are you cold? It's late, let's go back." The man didn't say anything, just dragged that hand to his mouth and kissed it.

The two walked back silently.

After arriving at the hotel, the man seemed still very excited, lying on an armchair, and the woman stood beside him, with an affectionate look, putting her hand to stroke the man's forehead, and gently asked him:

"Are you tired? Are you dizzy?"

The man then raised his head and looked at the woman's white face. For the fiftieth time, he said with a stubborn and childish look: "I love you."
